GRAND CENTER                                         RECORD OF PUBLIC MEETING
Date:                   Thursday, February 28, 2013
Time:                   6:00 p.m. to 8:00 p.m.
Location:               Storefront, 500 North Grand, St. Louis, MO 63103
Attendees:              Members of the Public
Meeting Purpose:        Public Meeting
Project:                Great Streets Grand Center
Project Number:         12082

Public Meeting Description / Purpose
The February 28, 2013 public open house was the first public meeting of the Great Streets Grand
Center Project. The meeting provided an opportunity for members of the public and community
stakeholders to share their vision of a more vibrant, attractive Grand Center. Planners listened to
attendees' desires for community improvements and beautification, such as better parking,
traffic, sidewalks, streets, landscaping, etc.

Meeting Location
The public open house was held in an unoccupied storefront located at 500 North Grand, St.
Louis, MO 63103.

Meeting Date
The public open house was held on Thursday, February 28, 2013.

Form Prepared By

Rebeccah Bennett of Vector Communications Corporation prepared this record of public
meeting. Vector Communications is responsible for public outreach and engagement for the
Great Streets Grand Center project.

6. Describe efforts to ensure citizen participation in the hearings, particularly by minorities
   and women.

      Targeted outreach to minorities included: 1) advertising in the St. Louis American newspaper
      and with First Civilizations, 2) residential and community outreach with Alderwoman

      There was no targeted outreach to ensure citizen participation by women.

   represented at the meeting? This should be based on staff observation.

      One hundred and three (103) people attended the public open house. Of these, 67 were
      women and 16 were recognizable people of color.

Public Meeting Description / Purpose
The May 9, 2013 public open house was the second public meeting of the Great Streets Grand
Center Project. The meeting provided an opportunity for community stakeholders and members
of the public to see new recommendations for making Grand Center a more vibrant and attractive
place to live, work, shop and play. Project team members delivered a 90-minute presentation
(followed by a question and answer period) on proposed improvements, including better lighting,
parking, streets, landscaping and beautification, traffic, transit access and more.

Meeting Location

The public open house was held in the auditorium of Cardinal Ritter College Preparatory High
School, located at 701 North Spring Ave., St. Louis, MO 63108.

Meeting Date

The public open house was held on Thursday, May 9, 2013.

I. Overview

1.1 Introduction

The Great Streets Grand Center Project is a six-month planning initiative sponsored by
Grand Center Inc. (GCI) and the East-West Gateway Council of Governments. Led by
Christner and Hoerr Schaudt, the planning process, involves hardscape and landscape
architects, transportation specialists, economic development experts, public art
professionals, public engagement consultants, community stakeholders and the public at-
large in a coordinated effort to enhance the social and economic vibrancy of the Grand
Center District. The resulting plan will build upon earlier work1 to improve the District's
overall design and function, with a specific focus on an area bounded by Cook to the
north, Olive to the south, Theresa to the east and Spring to the West. Once implemented,
the plan will aid the District in generating sustainable economic activity, creating a more
aesthetically pleasing sense of place, and maintaining attractive streets that serve all
modes of transportation.

1.2 Project Background

With its unique blend of performing arts, fine arts, music, media and educational
institutions, Grand Center is recognized locally and nationally as a cultural hub. It is an
established regional destination that aspires to be a thriving community in which people
of all backgrounds and interests come to live, work and play. To accomplish this, the
District must successfully resolve a host of practical and visual challenges that constrain
its growth and limit its appeal. The Great Streets Initiative provides a flexible framework
to address these challenges and to help the District realize its full potential.

1.3 Stakeholder & Public Involvement Plan ­ Purpose & Approach

Advancing Grand Center's "Arts & Life" vision requires the involvement of community
stakeholders and constituents throughout the planning process. The purpose of this
document is to present a comprehensive approach to engaging impacted stakeholders and
the general public in project planning efforts. As such, it describes goals, objectives and
tactics for advancing public awareness, comprehension, and participation in project
activities. These components form the project's Stakeholder & Public Involvement Plan
(SPIP) and are subject to modification in response to changing internal demands and
external realities.

Title VI of the Civil Rights Act of 1964

The content featured in this SPIP complies with all federal and state laws, regulations,
orders and directives regarding non-discrimination in federally assisted programs. Public
outreach, marketing and involvement efforts, including the development of promotional
materials and the hosting of public events will be conducted in compliance with Title VI
                                                                                                                
1
        Earlier work here is a reference to the Grand Center Framework Plan, which was completed in April 2012.


                                                                                                                                                                                        
                                                                                                                                                                                             11
                                                    

of the Civil Rights Act of 1964. The project team will work closely with East-West
Gateway throughout the planning process to ensure that environmental justice
requirements concerning minority and low-income persons are adequately and
appropriately addressed.

Guiding Principles

In addition to following Title VI statutes, the SPIP adheres to long-established public
involvement principles that inform the scope and design of the project's outreach and
engagement program. When practiced, these principles work to ensure that the program
1) adopts a process that is open and responsive to the different interests affected by
District planning efforts; and 2) yields meaningful stakeholder and public participation in
the project's decision-making. These principles, which include sustainability,
transparency, accessibility, representation and results, are expounded upon below.

       Sustainability:  Compels the project team to rely upon existing communications
       and outreach channels to raise awareness and involvement among community
       members and stakeholders. Working through established networks (like Grand
       Center's Plan Implementation Committee, Land Use Committee and various
       corridor committees) assures that trusted means of connection will be used to
       foster relationships with District stakeholders and affected publics.

       Transparency:    Works to make the planning process clear and easy to follow.
       The roles and responsibilities of the project team, stakeholder groups and the
       public at-large will be plainly and repeatedly articulated in order to manage
       expectations. Process participants will understand the part that they play in
       shaping the Great Streets plan. In addition, planning activities and events will be
       well publicized so that the public has ample notice of participation opportunities.

       Accessibility:   Maintains multiple points of entry into the planning process.
       Affected publics and stakeholder groups will be given a variety of ways to get
       involved from completing surveys to attending community charettes to
       participating in corridor committee meetings. No matter when people enter into
       the planning process, they will be able to understand the logic of events and
       activities. As a result, they will be able to participate with ease and can provide
       input at various stages of project decision-making.

       Representation:     Means that a broad range of stakeholder and community
       interests will be taken into consideration throughout the planning process.
       Citizens' issues, concerns and ideas will help guide plan outcomes. Here,
       representation is defined both in terms of demography ­ that is participants'
       physical and social characteristics (i.e. race, ethnicity, property ownership, etc.)
       and area of interest ­ that is what motivates participants to get involved (i.e.,
       residential, commercial, cultural, artistic and/or political concerns, etc.). This



                                                                                               
                                                                                                    12
                                                    

       approach attempts to invite all facets of the District, from the "easy to reach" to
       the "hard to reach" into the planning process.
       Results:  Focus the project team on implementing a proactive public involvement
       program that is aligned with Grand Center's project goals and effectively
       responds to community interests and needs.

By following these guiding principles, the project team will undertake a public
involvement process that facilitates constructive exchanges of information and ideas
between the public and the project's decision makers. This process will provide
community stakeholders with multiple opportunities to share their comments and
concerns about project objectives, activities and findings.




                                                                                              
                                                                                                   13
                                                    


II. Public Involvement Goals & Objectives

2.1 Involvement Program Goal

The central aim of the Great Streets ­ Grand Center public involvement program is to
obtain meaningful participation in the planning process by District stakeholders and
constituents. Accomplishing this requires that
stakeholders and the public have an appreciation of
planning parameters as well as an understanding of
major project decisions and their implications. More
specifically, meaningful participation is most likely
to occur when the involvement program
increases project awareness among stakeholders
and the public; stimulates people's interest in
plan activities and findings; deepens compre-
hension of the plan and its eventual outcomes; and
solicits constructive public input. These objectives
are described below in greater detail.

2.2 Involvement Program Objectives

Raising Awareness

Expanding the community's awareness of Grand Center's improvement efforts requires
the project team to provide clear, accurate and easily attainable information on the plan's
purpose, activities, and desired outcomes. To achieve this, the project team will:

    Develop and maintain excellent working relationships with GCI and East-West
    Gateway so that all public information needs are expertly addressed and proper
    communications protocols are followed;
    Participate in regular planning and coordination meetings with GCI and East-
    West Gateway to assure the accuracy of information products and communiqués;
    Employ a variety of communications vehicles to deliver reliable, timely project
    information to the public and stakeholders; and
    Work with local information outlets to maximize the plan's community exposure.

Generating Interest

While public information and awareness activities will deepen the community's
knowledge of the plan, they will not, by themselves, guarantee the public's interest in the
planning process. Getting people to care about the plan means first helping them to
understand how it impacts their quality of life. By focusing on the outcomes that matter
most to people like economic growth, improved patron experiences, better traffic flow,
and increased pedestrian activity, the team will shape a project identity that firmly
establishes the plan's relevance.


                                                                                           
                                                                                                14
                                                   



Promoting Understanding

Once District constituents are interested in the plan, the team will need to intensify its
explanation of project issues as well as deepen its comprehension of stakeholders' values,
needs and priorities. Through stakeholder and committee meetings and community
charrettes, the team will facilitate learning and sharing around key plan components,
including:

    First impression analysis (visual assessment of public realm and visitor
    experience),
    Traffic and parking (conditions, capacity, demand and supply),
    Utility/easement documentation (utility conditions, feasibility),
    Environmental data reports and as-built drawings,
    Pedestrian circulation (incidental meeting spots, gathering spaces and desire lines),
    ADA accessibility analysis (buildings, streets, routes, parking), and
    Bus and bike routes (bus stops, bike desire lines, bike storage).

Soliciting Input

The project team's work to educate the community about the District's Great Streets
planning effort will help prepare the public to provide meaningful input into the planning
process. The more informed stakeholders and community members are about the project,
the more likely they are to generate feedback that is helpful and insightful. To solicit
stakeholder and community input, the project team will:

    Meet with District stakeholder committees and institutions;
    Maintain open lines of communication with civic and business interests, elected
    officials, educational and faith based institutions, and neighborhood residents;
    Hold several days of community charrettes / workshops; and
    Employ a host of communication channels such as online surveys, comment
    forms, email messaging, newsletter inserts et.al.

Viewed broadly, this public involvement program is designed to cultivate stakeholder and
public trust in the planning process. This trust is fostered through an accountable and
responsive public involvement program that clearly connects the project's work to the
District's goals and needs.




                                                                                         
                                                                                              15
                                                    


III. Stakeholder Identification & Involvement Approach

3.1 Stakeholder Identification Procedures

One of the first and most critical steps of the SPIP is to identify project stakeholders. A
stakeholder is defined as any person or organization interested in or directly affected by
the project's activities. This usually includes, but is not limited to, residents or property
owners, neighborhood groups, business owners and operators, elected/community
officials, governmental resource agencies, special interest groups and religious and civic
institutions. Stakeholders for the Great Streets Grand Center Project have been identified
by GCI.

Below is a list of project stakeholders:

    Grand Center's 10 planning committees (comprised of major stakeholder
    institutions, District property owners, and municipal and state resource agencies):
        o Plan Implementation Committee
        o Land Use Committee
        o Art Walk Corridor Sub-Committee
        o Grand Boulevard Corridor Sub-Committee
        o Grandel Square Corridor Sub-Committee
        o Olive Street Corridor Sub-Committee
        o Spring Corridor Sub-Committee
        o Theresa Corridor Sub-Committee
        o Washington Corridor Sub-Committee
        o Technical Advisory Group
    Residential interests in and adjacent to the planning area. These include, but are
    not limited to:
        o Metropolitan Artists Lofts
        o Renaissance Place at Grand Apartments
        o University Plaza Apartments
        o Continental Life Building
        o Coronado Place Apartments & Lofts
        o Individual property owners
    Elected/community officials:
       o Alderwoman Marlene Davis, Ward 19
    Educational institutions:
       o St. Louis University
       o Harris Stowe State University
       o Parks College
       o Cardinal Ritter College Prep High School
       o Loyola Academy of St. Louis
       o Grand Center Arts Academy
       o Clyde Miller Career Academy



                                                                                             
                                                                                                  16
                                                    



    Religious organizations:
       o Third Baptist Church
       o Washington Tabernacle Church
       o Washington Metropolitan AME Zion Church
       o Central Baptist Church
       o Leonard Baptist Church
       o First Baptist Church
       o St. Alphonsus Liguori Rock Catholic Church
    Area hospitals:
       o John Cochran Veterans Administration Medical Center
    Civic/community organizations:
       o Grand Center Inc.
       o Urban League of Metropolitan St. Louis

The abovementioned stakeholders are among a larger group of impacted and interested
parties, more of whom will be identified through the project team's outreach and
engagement efforts. All stakeholders will be entered into the project's database so that
they can be kept abreast of project details and participation opportunities.

3.2 Stakeholder Involvement Expectations

Meaningful connections with project stakeholders will help the team develop a plan that
is community supported. Recognizing this, the team expects that stakeholders involved
in project planning will share their issues, concerns and priorities and help build public
interest and involvement in the plan. Input received from stakeholders and the public
will be incorporated into the plan's findings and considered by the project team.




                                                                                            
                                                                                                 17
                                                    


IV. Public Involvement Tools/Activities

The public involvement and communications activities presented on the following pages
describe the core work of the SPIP and are the primary means by which its goals and
objectives will be achieved. Responsibility for the coordination and execution of these
activities rests with the project team.

4.1 Public Involvement Tasks

Stakeholder & Public Involvement Plan

The Stakeholder & Public Involvement Plan (also referred to as the Community
Engagement Plan) will describe the range of activities the project team will undertake to
engage stakeholders and affected publics in plan development and decision-making. It
will also outline the goals and objectives of the involvement process; identify key
stakeholder groups; and clarify the specific communication strategies, meeting schedules
and expected outcomes of the engagement process.

Deliverables: Stakeholder & Public Involvement Plan
Accountable Party: Project Team
Timeframe: January 31, 2013
Associated Outreach: None required

Kick-off Meeting

The project team will participate in a project Kick-off meeting with members of Grand
Center's 10 planning committees and stakeholders of current District initiatives. The
purpose of this meeting is to:

       Update participants on the revisions to the Framework Plan;
       Introduce the members of the project team and briefly review their qualifications;
       Layout the principles and objectives of the Great Streets program; and
       Present the overall project schedule and responsibilities of the subcommittees.

Deliverables: Kick-off Meeting Minutes
Accountable Party: Project Team
Timeframe: January 9, 2013
Associated Outreach: Performed by GCI

Goals Summary / Great Streets Checklist

The project team will create a checklist that 1) incorporates the outcomes of the
Framework Plan with the principles of the Great Streets Program; and 2) articulates the
specific planning objectives that will govern project planning and design direction. This
checklist will also document the goals, priorities and strategies identified at the beginning
of the project and will be used throughout the planning process to evaluate concepts and


                                                                                           
                                                                                                18
                                                     

designs. In addition, the team will produce a summary of the project's goals and
continuously assess progress on these goals.

Deliverables: Goals Summary and Great Streets Checklist
Accountable Party: Project Team
Timeframe: January 30, 2013
Associated Outreach: None required

Committee Meetings

Select project team members will participate in two rounds of Grand Center planning
meetings with the District's six corridor subcommittees. The first round will follow the
project Kick-off meeting and will provide an opportunity for committee members to
review the Framework Plan's recommendations for the entire district and for their
corridors of interest. It will also give the project team a forum to listen to stakeholders'
issues and aspirations. Team members will use Framework Plan graphics and previous
meeting minutes to guide the discussion / listening sessions.

The second round of committee meetings will take place when the planning work is
roughly 75% complete. During these meetings, the project team will present its work to
date and solicit reactions and feedback.

Deliverables: Meeting Minutes, Outcomes & Team Direction
Accountable Party: Project Team
Round 1 Timeframe: January 10 & 11, 2013
Round 2 Timeframe: April 4 & 5, 2013 ­ Target Date
Associated Outreach: Performed by GCI

Stakeholder Interviews & Focus Group Meetings

Stakeholders currently undertaking planning efforts and capital improvements in the
District will be contacted for key informant interviews. Sixty to 90 minutes in length,
these interviews enable the project team to learn about plans and developments currently
underway and, where appropriate, to incorporate this information into the Great Streets
planning process. Six stakeholder interviews have been planned. They include:

   1.   John Cochran VA Medical Center ­ January 24, 2103
   2.   Alderwoman Marlene Davis (Ward 19) ­ Week of February 11, 2013
   3.   Grand Center Arts Academy ­ Week of February 11, 2013
   4.   Clyde Miller Career Academy ­ Week of February 18, 2013
   5.   St. Louis University ­ Week of February 18, 2013
   6.   Great Rivers Greenway District ­ Week of March 11, 2013

In addition to the stakeholder interviews, two focus groups will be held ­ one with
District residents and the other with area employees. These 90 minute meetings will help
the project team understand live / work priorities, interests and concerns in the District.



                                                                                            
                                                                                                 19
                                                     



The Resident Focus Group will be comprised of 12 to 15 District residents. Property
managers at the Renaissance Place at Grand Apartments, Metropolitan Artists Lofts,
University Plaza Apartments, Continental Life Building and Coronado Place Apartments
and Lofts will be asked to solicit the involvement of their tenants. Individual property
owners who live between Spring and Grand will also be invited to participate.

The Employee Focus Group will have between 15 to 20 participants who work at major
institutions located within the District. Grand Center's February PR/Communications
Network meeting, which is attended by area employees from major cultural and
educational institutions as well as local restaurants, is being repurposed so that the project
team can obtain planning insights from those who work in the District.

Deliverables: 6 Stakeholder Interviews, 2 Focus Groups and Interview/Meeting
Summaries
Accountable Party: Project Team
Interview Timeframe: See page 11
Focus Group Timeframe:
     Resident Focus Group: February 26, 2013 ­ Target Date
     Employee Focus Group: February 21, 2013
Associated Outreach: Performed by Project Team and GCI

Digital Survey and Analysis

The project team will develop digital survey questions directed toward area
patrons/volunteers, residents, students, employees and worshippers to obtain input on the
Distict's opportunities and challenges. An electronic survey will be submitted to GCI
and East-West Gateway for review and then administered two times ­ the first time to
establish baseline data that informs the plan's Great Streets criteria and the second time to
request input on the effectiveness of design solutions in meeting the criteria. The team
will analyze the survey findings and provide results to the project's sponsors.

Deliverables: Survey Questions & Response Analysis
Accountable Party: Project Team
Timeframe: Week of February 18, 2013 through Week of March 18, 2013
Associated Outreach: Performed by Emerson and GCI with input from Project Team

Community Charrette / Workshop

At the end of February, the project team will conduct a two day community charrette /
workshop. The charrette will be organized to allow subcommittee members, stakeholders,
Technical Advisory Group members and interested citizens access to the design team and
will help ensure their early participation in plan development. By the second week in
February, the project team will prepare an agenda and schedule for the charrette that
enables participants to explore a range of issues, focus areas and aesthetic preferences.
Team members will collect feedback from the charrette and will provide GCI and East-



                                                                                            
                                                                                                 20
                                                    

West Gateway a summary of findings and meeting minutes. Public notice of the
charrette will be placed in local media outlets to generate stakeholder and public
awareness.

Deliverables: Charrette Agenda, Schedule, Presentation & Materials, Findings &
Meeting Minutes
Accountable Party: Project Team
Timeframe: February 28, 2013 through March 1, 2013
Associated Outreach: Performed by GCI & Project Team

Technical Advisory Group (TAG) Meetings

Two TAG meetings will be held over the course of the planning process. The first
meeting is scheduled for after the project kick-off while the second meeting will take
place at the 75% design completion stage. The purpose of these meetings is to
understand the long-term transportation and utility needs of the District within the context
of the Framework Plan and the evolving District master plan. Input and insights from the
meeting will be captured and shared with the project's sponsors.

Deliverables: Meeting Minutes
Accountable Party: Project Team
Meeting 1 Timeframe: January 10, 2013
Meeting 2 Timeframe: April 4 or 5, 2013 ­ Target Date
Associated Outreach: Performed by GCI

Visual Arts Advisory Group Meeting

The project team will meet with the Visual Arts Advisory Committee one time to explore
the long-term challenges of art integration into the public realm. The timing of this
meeting will be linked to the availability of the artists and is yet to be determined. The
target for meeting with this group is near 50% design completion to allow the
incorporation of art opportunities into the design aesthetic. Team members will
summarize meeting findings.

Deliverables: Meeting Minutes
Accountable Party: Project Team
Timeframe: Requires further discussion and consideration
Associated Outreach: Performed by GCI

Land Use Committee Meeting

Grand Center's land use committee will meet once with the project team to review the
plan's preliminary findings as well as the recommendations of the market analysis. Team
members will document committee members' input and share it with GCI and East-West
Gateway.




                                                                                          
                                                                                               21
                                                  

Deliverables: Meeting Minutes
Accountable Party: Project Team
Timeframe: January 14, 2013 (initial meeting with GCI leaders) and April 4 or 5, 2013
(with Project Team) ­ Target Date
Associated Outreach: Performed by GCI

Final Presentation

A community presentation of the plan that includes a formal review of the plan's
components and an open discussion of findings will be held near the project's completion
to allow District stakeholders the opportunity to comment. The project team will capture
participants' feedback and include it in the project record.

Deliverables: PowerPoint Presentation & Presentation Boards, Meeting Comment
Summary
Accountable Party: Project Team
Timeframe: May 9, 2013 ­ Target Date
Associated Outreach: Performed by GCI

Scope & Capacity Building Session

The project team will meet with the Core Planning Team (which includes the plan's
sponsors), members of the TAG and other critical stakeholders to 1) review potential
phasing, funding and bundling of the identified work; 2) disclose cost estimates; and 3)
explain the critical linkages between work segments. As with all project meetings, a
summary of participants' comments will be developed and shared with project sponsors.

Deliverables: Meeting Minutes
Accountable Party: Project Team
Timeframe: May 9, 2013 ­ Target Date
Associated Outreach: Performed by GCI




                                                                                       
                                                                                            22
                                                 


V. Plan Monitoring

This Stakeholder and Public Involvement Plan (SPIP) will be regularly reviewed for
effectiveness and amended as appropriate. It is an "evergreen" document that may be
updated by the project team during the six-month planning period. Should the SPIP need
to be modified, team members will do so in a transparent manner that preserves the
integrity of the public involvement program.

              24
GREAT STREETS                                                 STAKEHOLDER
GRAND CENTER                                               MEETING SUMMARY
Date:                 Tuesday, February 5, 2013
Time:                 8:30 am
Location:             Grand Center Arts Academy
Attendees:            Lynne Glickert ­ Principal of GCAA, Dan Rubright - GCAA, Dan
                      Jay ­ Christner, Rachel Powers ­ Vector Communications
Meeting Purpose:      Stakeholder Interview
Project:              Great Streets Grand Center
Project Number:       12082

Introduction:
Dan Jay opened the meeting thanking Lynne and Dan for their time meeting with the
team. He then explained how the Great Streets process is building on the recently
completed Framework Plan. He also explained that this meeting is to dive deeper into
issues that affect Grand Center Arts Academy (GCAA), so that these issues can be
considered by the team and addressed in the process. He also discussed the team's
upcoming public open house, scheduled for Thursday, February 28, 2013 from 6:00 to
8:00 pm.

Question 1: What is the history of GCAA and where is GCAA going?
Answer: Lynne - Our staff had one year to get the school up and going. I went to Vince
Schoemehl to ask for use of the Grand Center name. We wanted to be called Grand
Center Arts Academy so that we could be ingrained in the center of the arts district. The
name wasn't proprietary, so we used it with Vince's approval. The first year of school
was held in the Baptist Church across Grand Ave. The current student population is 430,
with a maximum enrollment of 750 students.

GCAA's biggest challenge is being landlocked. Students and staff love being able to
walk to the arts organizations and that is what Dan works on most ­ partnerships. The
sidewalks don't work well for kids because they are too small. Our challenge is how to
dismiss a school of 750 kids with these small sidewalks and being landlocked.

With the excitement about this school, I don't lose sleep about the future of the school.
People are very excited about what we are doing here and we are really doing some great
things with these students. We have been able to be very flexible with addressing issues
that arise. I am excited to be a place where the kids can be their quirky selves without
being ostracized. These kids have now settled into a place where they aren't thought of as
strange.

Question 2: How big is your staff?
Answer: Lynne ­ We have 47 staff members ­ including custodial staff, and part time
and full time teachers. When we get to 750 students, we will have about 80 staff
including some part time employees.



                                                                                          
                                                                                               25
Dan R. ­ As we build more partnerships and expand our faculty and after school
programs, we will be expanding the extra special arts focus of the school, including
media like filmmaking.

One thing we are working on is how to get more levels of art engagement in Grand
Center. There seems to be a frequency range of the organizations working in Grand
Center. There is a high frequency with Pulitzer and symphony type organizations. There
seems to be a high level of group think when it comes to this district and the arts
programs offered. Then you have a lower frequency range where we fit. Craft Alliance is
more aligned with us because we both focus on education and outreach. We want to have
more cross talk between the frequencies. It's all a matter of how the organizations see
their assets. We are trying to think through how we can get the upper frequencies to see
how they can work with the lower frequencies to do more engagement and programming
on a wider scale. Their thinking seems to be "we have our show then let out and it's
over" versus thinking that there are a lot of levels of art opportunities that people can be
engaged in. We are looking at art from a sidewalk chalk level all the way up. Art is
everywhere and it doesn't have to just be through the shows, it can be more engaging.

Question 3: What percentage of students come in vehicles by parents?
Answer: Lynne - Most students are brought to school by their parents since we don't
provide transportation. About 5% of students at this point ride public transportation. All
the staff park behind Powell Hall where the Circus Flora tent is usually set up. Fifteen
percent of students come from St. Louis County, which is part of the problem. With the
gas prices, we are starting to see some of those students not return to school. The
commuting price is too high for some of them. We are trying to look at carpools and
public transportation, but those efforts haven't caught on yet.

Question 4: In the afternoon, what is pick up like at 3:30?
Answer: Lynne - Currently we take all kids across Grand Ave to the parking lot and the
parents pick them up there. When the weather is bad, we don't have a plan B. We've had
the streets department come in and they haven't been able to come up with a plan. They
look at our issue and say, "yep you have a problem."

Dan R. ­ The symphony hates it and it is a big problem that's getting worse. I've been
out at events and people from the Symphony have mentioned the issue to me.

Lynne ­ There are probably 200 cars on that back lot at 3:30 pm. Some of them park on
Samuel Shepard and the kids walk down to meet them. We used to use the space near the
Sun Theatre, but since they have started construction we can't use that space any more.

Question 5: Will you do pick up shifts?
Answer: Lynne - We might try that next year, but we can't really do that easily because
of parents with kids in multiple grades. As we increase our robust afterschool program
we will eliminate the issue more, but it's going to really be an issue no matter how we
stagger our dismissal.




                                                                                              
                                                                                                   26
Dan R.­ If we can project data about the number of cars we are dealing with, will that
really help?

Dan J. - Yes, if you could give us the numbers of vehicles that you see, it will be very
useful. This is an urban situation and congestion comes from urban situations so we
won't solve it all, but we should anticipate it and build it into the plan.

Lynne ­ We love the idea of opening our doors, having a green space and having a turn
around at the Sun Theatre. All high schools you look at have very open spaces. A concern
for us is having a space for students to safely linger during dismissal. They are so social
that they don't want to leave after school and we are often shooing them toward their
waiting parents or buses when they want to stick around talk with their friends. They
often don't get to interact with other kids that are like them in their neighborhood or
home environment, so this time with their friends - they really enjoy it.

Dan R. ­ As we think about after school programs, we should look at them as
disbursement programs as well ­ if we can keep at least 1/3 of the students at least one
hour after school we could potentially disperse more efficiently.

My idea is possibly a tunnel that goes underneath Grand from here to the Powell side so
people don't ever have to think about crossing Grand Ave to get to the other side. Grand
is really just a highway. I have lots of pictures in my phone of accidents, people being hit
by cars; a student was dinged by a car. I think about how do you get people through
Grand in a fun and light-hearted way? A tunnel is one way to do it.

Lynne ­ We have teachers who think they are risking their lives at the end of the school
day. There has got to be a way for us to think about going west for our dismissal. There is
so much less traffic that direction and I do worry about it. We just don't have a good
system now even with teachers in vests, crossing guards, or the zebra stripes on the street.
Most people don't even pay attention to the zebra stripes, they just speed right through
them ­ even though they are supposed to stop for pedestrians.

Dan R. ­ Chances are the VA will max out Delmar going west and we don't know about
this street {Grandel Square} and Grand will always be a danger.

Question 6: Up to the edge of the Sun where the parking lot is, who owns that?
Answer: Lynne - We are not sure, each time we ask we get a different answer. We also
don't really know what they are planning to do with the Urban League lot and the drive
through. There was talk of a swap.

Question 7: Would you ever do something where you could have staff accompany
kids on the bus to the Metrolink ­ possibly a shuttle or articulated bus?
Answer: Lynne ­ I don't think any of our kids take that Metrolink. But, it's not
uncommon to have the bus that stops close by from the South to be half filled with our
kids. Some others use the Delmar bus (about 12 from east and 15 from west). You are
right, the reason urban schools work is because of transit.



                                                                                            
                                                                                                 27
Dan J. ­ You have to think about taking a proactive role to get people to think about
transit as a very viable option. Maybe there is a teacher that lives in the area and if the
kids are on the bus by 7:30 am then they will ride with the teacher.

Lynne ­ That's a good idea, we never thought about it that way, but that's a great idea.

Dan R. ­ As kids get in high school, some of them can ride their bike to the Metrolink.

Question 7: I want to learn more about green space. Tell me about your future
vision there?
Answer: Lynne ­ The only green space we have is currently behind the building. If you
exit behind the building and go behind the Sun Theatre, you will see an area we planted.
We are working with the Lawrence Group to figure out what can be done with that space.
Other potential green space is the Beaux Arts side of the building. The second floor is
crying out for a container gardening. Our only space for physical activity is currently
studios. We try to keep a good relationship with Cardinal Ritter, so we have used their
football field before if we have something that requires a large outdoor space. They have
been good at letting us use their space. One time we had a large balloon launch as part of
a science project and we went to the football field, but we wouldn't be able to do that
here.

Dan R. ­ We've been thinking about a way to have more space where the kids can get out
and move around and get some physical education. We've also been talking to Father
Bussi about his space. We've planted a garden near the Sun Theatre but it will become
passive space due to construction. Father Biondi says we can use some of St. Louis
University's space to plant in their planters ­ that's one way to get some green
interaction. I've been wondering how can we have green space for events.

Question 8: The space west of the Sun Theatre ­ what if it were a double duty pick
up zone in the evening and play area during the day? That way it gives you the
opportunity for release that's not parked up by anybody.
Answer: Dan R. ­ I like the idea.

Dan J. ­ If you use it as a parking solution, then it will not be a maximum use of the
space. Maybe Steve Smith could look at this for you. I would encourage you to not let
the parking challenge wag the dog.

Lynne ­ I really like that solution much more. It feels like that concept expands the
footprint of our school in a much better way.

Dan J. ­ It's an urban playground. It's not without it's challenges, but you can talk with
Steve and his team about that.




                                                                                               
                                                                                                    28
Lynne ­ It's no reason that with the drive through concept it can be there for a certain
period of time and the rest of the time it is closed off for pedestrians. I think that idea has
some real potential there.

Dan J. ­ this is one of those problems that's going to take twenty solutions because it's
the urban environment. We just need to make sure we are not letting parking dictate over
the needs of the kids and the school.

Question 9: How can we get information to your parents and staff to get them
involved in this planning process, in particular the upcoming charrettes?
Answer: Lynne ­ GCAA's and Cardinal Ritter's parents are both very unique
populations that have a lot to share. Our parents would love to get involved in this
planning. Most of them don't live in this area, but they come down here everyday and
would love to spend more time here.

When we had our grand opening, we asked parents to come and participate in a "plan
your city" activity and they really got into it and had some great ideas. So, I know they
would be really engaged with this process.

Dan R. ­ I think I am going to have a separate meeting with them to update parents and
staff about the plan. Often, they don't get the information about what is going on in the
district on that level, but they will be very enthusiastic and engaged with this process.

                                                                                                    29
GREAT STREETS                                                     STAKEHOLDER
GRAND CENTER                                                  MEETING SUMMARY
Date:                  Tuesday, February 5, 2013
Time:                  3:00 pm
Location:              St. Louis City Hall, Room 230
Attendees:             Alderwoman Marlene Davis, Dan Jay ­ Christner, Rebeccah
                       Bennett ­ Vector Communications
Meeting Purpose:       Stakeholder Interview
Project:               Great Streets Grand Center
Project Number:        12082

Introduction:
Dan Jay opened the meeting thanking Alderwoman Davis for her time. He then
explained how the Great Streets process is building on the recently completed Framework
Plan. He also discussed the team's upcoming public open house, scheduled for Thursday,
February 28, 2013 from 6:00 to 8:00 pm.

1. Question: What is the current perception of Grand Center?
Answer: Grand Center is seen as a vibrant, exciting place for people to live, work and
come play. It used to be lifeless without much energy. There was very little variety in
terms of retail and dining amenities. Now, the area has 12 restaurants and thriving
cultural institutions. It is also an educational hub of the region. You can find educational
institutions in every part of the community, ranging from higher education to elementary
school.

While the area is exciting, there is still room to grow. We need more residents, more
retail and maybe even another mid-sized entertainment venue that would hold 1,000 to
1,200 patrons. The area also needs more diversity. This may come as a result of
attracting a larger variety of retail institutions.

I'd like to see this community become more of a regional and national destination place.
In terms of accomplishing this, Sweetie Pies has helped to put our community on the
map.

2. Question: What are the biggest changes that you'd like to see in Grand Center in
the near future?
Answer: I'd like to see more residential housing in the neighborhood. The true
boundaries of the community go to Page. Near Page, we have a new Save A Lot, PNC
Bank, Walgreens and St. Louis Housing Authority corporate office. There's also a new
coffee shop there.

3. Question: How can Great Streets help spur community improvements?
Answer: People need more comfort. They need streets that are passable. Sidewalks
need to be in good condition. Traffic flow needs to be improved. Also, there should be
more lighting for public safety. In addition to all of this, I'd like to see great signage for



                                                                                                  
                                                                                                       30
our venues that communicates vibrancy and that is easy to see from a distance. We are
an entertainment district and we need flexibility with signage.

Beautification is also really important. We don't need anything over the top, but the
community needs to be made more inviting, engaging and comfortable. One way of
doing this has less to do with landscaping and more to do with human connections. Our
district needs area guides, like they have downtown. These people could be positioned
throughout the community and could direct people to events, activities, venues,
restaurants etc. This would give people the opportunity to do more than they normally
would and could greatly enhance our retail environment.

4. Question: How do we engage the surrounding neighborhoods?
Answer: Few residents live in the Grand Center District proper. There are some to the
west on Grandel Square who are always upset and feel as though they should control
everything. Northwest on Cook, Finney and Windsor we have Covenant Blu residents.
Some are first time homebuyers. They generally like living close to everything and have
developed a strong sense of community. This area is also anchored by older churches
and community minded pastors who look for opportunities to get involved (especially at
Fresh Bible). On the east side of Grand is Renaissance Place, which has public,
affordable and market rate housing. This area has a great support system through Urban
Strategies along with a community center on Delmar. Within walking distance of
Renaissance Place is Kim's Kids (a day care center), the Symphony, St. Alphonsus Rock
Church and others. There are also businesses behind Grand that have been in the
community for 40 to 50 years (ex. American Auto and Sun's Chinese).

5. Question: How do we preserve the neighborhood's stability and bring about
change?
Answer: You must engage stakeholders who really care about the community. They are
willing to do whatever it takes to make the area stronger and better as long as they can be
part of the change and aren't going to be forced out.

6. Question: How do we get more community participation in the planning
process?
Answer: GCI hired Rose Terranova and she is definitely a great resource. Also, a
number of the venues and institutions in the area are now doing more community
outreach because it's good for business and their long-term viability. We are making
progress on this front, but we still have a long ways to go. You all must explain how
your process will add to and not take from the community. Also, be sure to engage faith
leaders like Rev. Dr. Rodney Frances of Washington Tabernacle. Other area churches
include Central Baptist, Progressive, St. Alphonsus Rock etc. I'm also willing to
distribute information about the open house to my constituents.

7. Question: What are the greatest challenges facing this project?
Answer: Implementing anything is a potential problem here. There could be adverse
impacts on businesses, patrons and others, so we must be very thoughtful and careful in
how we proceed. It's important to get buy-in from institutional stakeholders, many of



                                                                                           
                                                                                                31
whom may have divergent agendas. Focus on the positive benefits of giving the area new
life like better access, greater safety, new and enhanced lighting, improved sustainability
etc. All of this, taken together, can outweigh the challenges.

8. Question: What are the qualities of the Grand Center District that must be
preserved and enhanced?
Answer: Arts and cultural institutions like the Arts and Entertainment Council and St.
Louis Artworks need to be preserved. These mid-sized and small organizations are
critical to the areas vibrancy and must not be pushed out.

Action Items:

       Find out from Brenda Fenky whether or not the charrette space is actually
       available or if the build out is proceeding in February.
       Once flyers are created, send them to Alderwoman Davis for distribution and
       dissemination.




                                                                                          
                                                                                               32
GREAT STREETS                                                   STAKEHOLDER
GRAND CENTER                                                MEETING SUMMARY
Date:                  Friday, February 8, 2013
Time:                  1:30 pm
Location:              St. Louis University
Attendees:             Peg Weathers ­ St. Louis University, Assistant Vice President for
                       Community Relations, Dan Jay ­ Christner, Laurel Harrington ­
                       Christner, Rebeccah Bennett ­ Vector Communications
Meeting Purpose:       Stakeholder Interview
Project:               Great Streets Grand Center
Project Number:        12082

Introduction:
Dan Jay opened the meeting thanking Peg Weathers for her willingness to meet with the
team. He explained that stakeholder interviews provide an opportunity for team
members to learn the opportunities and challenges facing the Grand Center community.

1. Question: What is the current perception of Grand Center?
Answer: Our students don't even cross the street into Grand Center and this isn't true of
only underclassmen. Graduate students behave the same way. Our students spend time
on Laclede's Landing, visit Soulard and hang out on Locust, but they don't cross the
street into Grand Center.

2. Question: What is the university's interest in Grand Center?
Answer: Our view of Grand Center has changed over time. Father Biondi has been
involved with GCI forever. We're pro-commerce. Active businesses provide safety for
our students. The more thriving properties there are around us, the better the safety
prospects. A vibrant Grand Center also makes for a more appealing place for students'
parents. Our student development office delivers a message to student prospects about
the area when conducting introductions to the university. This is a far cry from how
things used to be. In the past, we stated in our orientation packets not to cross Lindell.
Clearly, our messages about the surrounding community have changed.

What we care about most is the safety of our students as we deliver an exceptional
educational experience. Safety in the neighborhood used to be a big concern, but now the
perception of safety is a bigger issue than safety itself.

3. Question: Are you familiar with the Framework Plan?
Answer: I've attended two Framework Plan meetings ­ one at the Symphony and the
other at the Scottish Rite.
Background Information (Dan & Laurel): The Framework Plan offers a basic strategy
for moving Grand Center forward and includes narrowing streets, shifting traffic flow,
redesigning parking etc. What we're doing now with the Great Streets project is taking
the plan to the next level of detail. We're validating the basic ideas behind the plan, but
building on its recommendations to prepare for eventual implementation.



                                                                                          
                                                                                               33
4. Question: Are you familiar with the Art Walk?
Answer: Yes, though I don't know where things stand right now.
Background Information (Dan & Laurel): The Art Walk currently includes the SLU
Gallery, Scottish Rite, Public Media Commons, the Sheldon, CAM, Pulitzer and ends at
the burnt church. This is a change from the walk's original design because it includes the
major arts institutions. The second change to the walk involves a new Great Rivers
Greenway (GRG) trail. The trail will follow the old Hodiamont Street car line. GRG is
looking at connecting the trail to the St. Vincent's Greenway and to the Grand Center
District ­ possibly at the burnt church.

5. Question: What are the biggest changes that you'd like to see in Grand Center in
the near future?
Answer: Traffic congestion and street design are major issues. With regard to traffic,
Vandeventer and Compton are how I get into and out of the district these days. I don't
travel down Grand anymore because of the congestion, especially during rush hour.

My issues with street design have to do first and foremost with the size of Lindell.
Lindell is so massive, that it's like a canyon. What can we do to make this more
manageable? Sidewalk to sidewalk it's just so large, which creates a major barrier. My
second design concern deals with streetscape once you're in the district. I've walked up
to City Diner and to Dooley's for lunch, but from the corner of Lindell and Grand to City
Diner, the street is dark and unappealing. The front of the Fox is funky. Craft alliance
sort of sucks, the neon is pretty, but the windows are unappealing. The whole walk is not
interesting. It's a buzz kill. There's very little that's visually engaging and appealing.

6. Question: How do we make this area a major asset for the campus that it's
proud of and publicly connects to?
Answer: You may want to involve Steve Smith in these conversations. He has a great
relationship with Father Biondi and is a trusted informal advisory. His lobbying will
really be important on getting changes made to Theresa. He's one of the best outside
representatives to the university on anything having to do with development. Also, I
think Joe Adorjan is on Grand Center's board and he's a SLU trustee and a dear friend of
Father Biondi's. He was the chairman of our board when he was chair of GCI's board.
Steve and Joe are the guys to deliver what you need or want from SLU to Father. Also,
be sure to include Peter Pierotti. Peter is where you start on anything having to do with
the university's buildings, property and real estate. Peter knows about the university's
plans east of Theresa.

7. Question: What else do you think that we need to know?
Answer: I talked to Father Biondi a long time ago about the Art Walk and he said that
he was willing to talk about it. Peter's talked to him about the concept and I think he
continues to be supportive. The question will always be how much money do you want
from us, are you taking our property and what's this do to the safety of our students.
Sometimes connections to the community aren't a strong appeal for us because we're
worried that our students may adversely be affected and safety always comes first with
us.



                                                                                        
                                                                                             34
Additionally, we care about how these new Grand Center developments can help us
improve the quality of the students we attract. We're interested in learning what other
Jesuit institutions located in urban areas are doing with regard to "town-gown"
interactions and developments.

Lastly, we have a large institutional footprint. We have 4,000 employees here as well as
11 or 12,000 students.

8. Question: Who should we connect with to get SLU students and Parks College
students to participate in the project's electronic survey?
Answer: Contact student development. This is Ken Porterfield's office (he's a VP).
Send me an email and I'll find the right person and get you to him or her.




                                                                                           
                                                                                                35
GREAT STREETS                                                 STAKEHOLDER
GRAND CENTER                                               MEETING SUMMARY
Date:                 Wednesday, February 13, 2013
Time:                 9:00 am
Location:             Clyde C. Miller Academy
Attendees:            Brandon Murray ­ Assistant Principal ­ Clyde C. Miller Academy,
                      Dan Jay ­ Christner, Rachel Powers ­ Vector Communications
Meeting Purpose:      Stakeholder Interview
Project:              Great Streets Grand Center
Project Number:       12082

Introduction:
Rachel Powers opened the meeting thanking Mr. Murray for taking the meeting in
Principal Warmack's absence. (Principal Warmack called in sick for the day. Team
members were not notified before arriving at the school). She discussed the team's
upcoming public open house, scheduled for Thursday, February 28, 2013 from 6:00 to
8:00 pm.

Dan Jay then explained how the Great Streets process is building on the recently
completed Framework Plan.

Question 1: What is the history of Clyde C. Miller (CCM)?
Answer: Clyde C. Miller is a school of choice/magnet school. It was started as a
construction career academy and evolved into a career, technical and college ready
training school, which then evolved into a pathways learning program. There are 13
pathways that students choose from when they enter. We were the first high school with
the dual enrollment of high school curriculum combined with a career and technical
focus. Now there are other schools in the region with the same dual track, so we are not
as unique, but we were the first.

There are post-secondary prep classes that are unique to this school ­ the most functional
path is the Certified Nurses Assistant (CNA) program that allows students to take the test
at age 18 and become licensed. Educators are finding that there are more benefits to this
model than a regular high school model. One reason we are successful is that all seniors
have A and B days where they are off campus doing their internships with some partner
job sites. We have great partners and our students are getting hands on experience before
they even graduate. So they leave here with a leg up already.

Question 2: What is your student population and graduation rate like?
Answer: College placement in 2011 was approximately 89 ­ 93%. We have 796 enrolled
students (9th ­ 12th). We've seen a decrease in enrollment in the last 2 years. We used to
be very selective with enrollment, with a mandatory interview, essay and application
process. Now, we have had to hit the enrollment numbers to keep our budget, so we have
changed our enrollment process slightly. Instead of being as selective as we had been, we
are taking a chance on more individuals. The other reason for decreased numbers is that
the pool of kids is really smaller ­ kids are transferring to the county more in search of


                                                                                        
                                                                                             36
more options. The first four weeks of school we comb our list and go get the kids that we
were expecting to show up but didn't. Often there is a simple mistake with them knowing
where they were supposed to go. The superintendent is really trying to put a stop to inter-
district transfers ­ to the county. Last year, I actually suggested that we go up to the
alternative school and review their list. We saw a few kids who we decided to give a
second chance and enrolled them in our school. This wasn't a popular solution, but those
kids have really stepped up and appreciated that second chance and they are doing great
here.

Question 3: What are your Full Time Equivalent (FTE) staff numbers?
Answer: FTE staff is 76 (54 classroom teachers; the rest are support staff). Hitting our
enrollment numbers is so critical because if we lose ~ 40 kids, it would cost us a teachers
position.

Question 4: What is your transportation like?
Answer: We have a bus system ­ 26 buses through First Student school bus. Eighty
percent of students ride these buses; about 15% ride the Metrobus or walk; 3% have a
parent drop them off and pick them up; and the remaining 2 to 3% drive, which is about
20-25 students. CCM is a first tier school ­ busses drop off at 6:25 am ­ they work three
bus drop off times for the high school, middle school, then elementary.

Question 5: What is your staff parking situation like ­ do they all park on the lot
behind the school?
Answer: Our parking lot is more than sufficient to accommodate staff ­ it's a luxury of
this school that we have about 122 parking spaces.

Question 6: What is the relationship with CCM and Grand Center?
Answer: It's an interesting dynamic, anyone familiar with the neighborhood knows that
CCM sits as a central piece of Grand Ave ­ from us down south it's full of life, great
food, historic, going north it's less maintained, not safe for our kids, etc. There are
resources south that we could use more, we have used SLU's kids as mentors for tutoring
­ they are one of our biggest resources, some kids have gone to the FOX. The other piece
is that Cardinal Ritter is close, Vashon is close ­ there could be fighting issues and we've
had to issue no trespassing orders to keep our kids from going to their schools and their
kids from coming to ours.

Also, because we are centrally located we often have spectators that just want to come to
our sporting events and watch so that adds to our crowds. There is a lot of traffic all
around the school all the time. As for the neighborhood, our kids understand the
territorial rights of the streets better than anyone ­ there are blocks they don't walk down.
I've been to Roosevelt and other schools - and I don't feel unsafe here at all.

Question 7: How is the diversity of the school population?
Answer: We are not as diverse as other schools. We have a large African American
student population, few white students; minuscule numbers of Asian students; and almost
no Middle Eastern students. Other schools going north have larger Bosnian populations



                                                                                           
                                                                                                37
and other ethnicities. Just walking through, someone could label this as a predominantly
African American school. I think this is mostly because we are so far north, where the
south city area has more diversity pockets.

Question 8: What is the street traffic situation like for you?
Answer: It's a fairly busy hub. There is not a day you don't see people walking up and
down Grand. I think it's safe, but my take is that I make my own assumptions about
where I am. My first thing I do is to walk the neighborhood and get a feel for what it
looks like, whose out and about, what do you see. There is a busy park not far from here,
we have a track out back and people come from the apartments and walk our track for
exercise. There is some gang activity not far from us ­ it doesn't really affect us. If the
gangs have issues we don't see it out and about a lot. At another school I worked for,
when the gangs had issues, it impacted our students. There was violence all the time.
There are violent issues here, but it seems that these students are given the same respect
as the FOX and other institution's patrons.

Question 9: In your opinion, what should this part of Grand become ­ what's
possible here to make this a place where people stay and possibly live or should it
just be an institutional corridor?
Answer: Right now it's all about perception. The current perception about the
neighborhood is that it is not a nice neighborhood. People don't come pass the FOX
because they think we are in the middle of the ghetto. There are many things this
neighborhood has to offer.

One issue is the old Carver School behind us that's not being used ­ we'd love to see that
as a regulation size field and track of our own. We are one of the most successful athletic
programs in our conference, but we don't have large enough facilities to encourage sports
participation. Put an athletic field there to hold district games and it draws lots of people
­ locals also come.

A grocery store down this way would be helpful too ­ something like Aldi's. We need
more sit down restaurants down in this area. Church's is very busy. The problem with
getting some of these developments is that developers see low income housing and it
scares them away because they don't think they could make money, but it's not that way
at all. Most complaints I hear from people in the neighborhood and students are why
couldn't we have something like that in our neighborhood. I'll say, last year I walked into
Church's Chicken for lunch right in the middle of it being robbed ­ that's the issue that
we have to overcome because the perception is that there is a possibility of that
happening all the time!

So I'm saying to get residents more active and change the perception of the area, we need
larger athletic facilities, more retail and restaurant opportunities. For example, I love the
Iron Barley bar at 16th Street and I-55, the food is great, the area and safety is
questionable after dark, but it's always busy ­ you know why - it's perception.




                                                                                           
                                                                                                38
Question 10: How is this area of Grand differentiating itself from Grand Center
with a major high school and major hospital?
Answer: I don't know, I think people are so unfamiliar with this piece of real estate we
get visitors who don't realize we are a school. A lot of people are turned off by the VA
hospital being across the street due to the perception of them being war veterans with
mental health issues, and the facilities being dirty.

Along Grand Ave. people don't mind being around college kids, but they don't really like
being around teenagers and high school kids

While I don't agree with this, people's perception is that it's a high school with 800 black
kids. You could flip us with Cardinal Ritter where people perceive them as a private
school, with paid tuition and they must be better and well behaved. But we've had just as
many of their kids come here for a fight after school and have had to escort them off the
premises. Many parents come here and use the other facilities because they have kids
here. This area would be different, but I'm not sure how, but it will have a different feel.

It's the individuals who live here that have the most important input because they will
have to support what's being done here. The people in this neighborhood are people who
enjoy being in close proximity to everything that they need. Bringing in more things is
what they want. I wonder how many of these neighborhood people have actually gone
inside the FOX for a show or simply a tour. Maybe it's because they (the FOX) market to
and advertise with markets that don't really hit the street. Maybe it's because they do not
feel welcome? I took kids to the Black Rep to see Othello and they loved it. I'm a
Chicago guy but St. Louis stays so divided. These institutions only cater to a certain kind
of person instead of looking at how we could kick open the doors and be so much more. I
don't understand why this couldn't happen more. It can be done. You have to do the
legwork and ground work and interact with different people. It's all going back to the
perception that if we open our doors to all kinds of people - can we be successful?

People have a perception of St. Louis City Public Schools also. We have some of the
most professional and intelligent staff that you could ever meet. People don't think large
fights happen in St. Charles but they do and 11 students were suspended. If people come
in and see us they will see we have 100% graduation rate and 80-90% college placement
rate. On a Wednesday afternoon you go to Mike Shannon's for lunch and two of our kids
are interning there. What is an inner city school ­ it's just a school within the city limits.

I would love to have an electronic marquee to highlight our accomplishments out on the
corner of Grand Ave. It's also key to develop more media relationships. People want
this area to be built up; everyone says this was one of the most beautiful inner cities in the
region. This community is full of people who love this area and want to stay here and see
it be built back up.

Question 11: How can we get the word out to your parents, staff and community
about the planning process and upcoming charrettes?




                                                                                            
                                                                                                 39
Answer: We can send out an email flyer, do a phone blast to all of our parents. We could
also send an email or flyer to our internship business partners who would love to see
what's going on and be part of the process. We have a pretty engaged parent community
with about 40 to 100 parents attending our PTO meetings. That's pretty good for a St.
Louis Public high school.

Action Items:

Electronic flyer for email blast
Printed flyer for distribution
Script for call blast to parents

GREAT STREETS                                     EMPLOYEE FOCUS GROUP
GRAND CENTER                                          MEETING SUMMARY
Date:                 Thursday, February 21, 2013
Time:                 10:00 am
Location:             Metropolitan Artists Lofts, Community Room
Attendees:            Grand Center Area Employees
Meeting Purpose:      Employee Focus Group
Project:              Great Streets Grand Center
Project Number:       12082

Overview
On Thursday, February 21, 2013, 16 people who work in or near the Grand Center
District met with members of the Great Streets project team to share their perceptions of
the community's assets, challenges and needs. As part of this process, team members
explained the Great Streets project; solicited background information from attendees via
a written survey; and conducted a facilitated discussion of 10 project related questions.
The insights from the survey and group discussion are presented in this document, though
participants' comments remain confidential.           Team members and community
stakeholders will use the findings from this summary to inform the project's planning
process and decision-making.

Discussion Findings
After focus group participants submitted their brief surveys, project team members
engaged them in facilitated discussions about their Grand Center experiences. They were
asked questions about their perceptions of the area, the qualities and characteristics of the
neighborhood that should be enhanced, the challenges they encounter working in the
district, frequent travel / traffic conditions, their transportation choices, and the work and
non-work amenities they would like the area to have. Their responses to these questions
have been compiled and are presented in the tables on the following pages.

GREAT STREETS                                          RESIDENT FOCUS GROUP
GRAND CENTER                                               MEETING SUMMARY
Date:                    Tuesday February 26, 2013
Time:                    6:00 pm
Location:                Metropolitan Artist Loft Community Room
Attendees:               Grand Center Area Residents, Laurel Harrington ­ Christner,
                         Rachel Powers ­ Vector Communications
Meeting Purpose:         Residential Focus Group
Project:                 Great Streets Grand Center
Project Number:          12082

Overview
On Tuesday, February 26, 2013, 12 people who live in or near the Grand Center District
met with members of the Great Streets project team to share their perceptions of the
community's assets, challenges and needs. As part of this process, team members
explained the Great Streets project; solicited background information from attendees via
a written survey; and conducted a facilitated discussion of nine project related questions.
The insights from the survey and group discussion are presented in this document, though
participants' comments remain confidential. Team members and community
stakeholders will use the findings from this summary to inform the project's planning
process and decision-making.

Survey Findings

                            BACKGROUND INFORMATION SURVEY

Discussion Findings

After focus group participants submitted their brief surveys, project team members engaged them in
facilitated discussions about their Grand Center experiences. They were asked questions about their
perceptions of the area, the qualities and characteristics of the neighborhood that should be enhanced, the
challenges they encounter living in the district, frequent travel / traffic conditions, their transportation
choices, and the residential amenities they would like the area to have. Their responses to these questions
have been compiled and are presented in the tables on the following pages.

                  TRANSPORTATION OPTIONS & EXPERIENCES
What is your experience leaving Grand Center?
 Traffic on Grand Ave. in the evenings and weekends is "crazy"
 Police chases occur down Grand Ave. is a safety concern
 Ambulances along Grand Ave. cause congestion
 Sport bike drag racing on Grand Ave. at night after midnight is a nuisance

What is your experience returning to Grand Center?
 Fox traffic in the evenings cause residents to divert to different routes or wait extra
  time to enter district

What parking issues have you experienced?
 Too many sporadic lots and no centralized parking system
 Too many meters
 Not enough residential parking available

What are you views of We Car?
 4 of 9 respondents would utilize We Car
 More convenient than public transit - especially if shopping
 Easily accessible
 Affordable
 Provides another back up option if main vehicle is out of commission

Art Walk Committee                                                           Grand Center
January 10, 2013 Discussion Summary                                   Great Streets Project

Overview
The Art Walk Committee met with members of the Great Streets (GS) team on Thursday,
January 10, 2013. Ten committee members and Grand Center Inc. (GCI) representatives
participated in the meeting, which was held to accomplish the following objectives:
    Acquaint committee members with the Great Streets team;
    Provide the team with information on the committee's work to date; and
    Identify critical corridor issues that the team needs to consider during the planning
    process.
A list of meeting attendees is presented below.

 Overview of      Don, Framework Plan:
 framework ­      When we started off the plan itself or the framework plan the initial
 discussion of    concept "steeple to steeple" had been introduced much earlier. I said
 school parking   let's keep our area dealing with as small an area as possible to focus
                  efforts. I began to focus on the area from Olive to Delmar thinking

                  the symphony, the academy, Third Baptist, Grandel, Fox,
