Olive Street Corridor Sub-Committee                                          Grand Center
January 10, 2013 Discussion Summary                                    Great Streets Project

Overview
The Olive Street Corridor Sub-Committee met with members of the Great Streets (GS)
team on Thursday, January 10, 2013. Seven committee members and Grand Center Inc.
(GCI) representatives participated in the meeting, which was held to accomplish the
following objectives:
    Acquaint committee members with the Great Streets team;
    Provide the team with information on the committee's work to date; and
    Identify critical corridor issues that the team needs to consider during the planning
    process.
A list of meeting attendees is presented below.

Attendance

Committee Members & GCI Representatives:
Matthew Foggy                  Property Owner / Resident
Paul DeMerath                  Scottish Rite Cathedral Preservation Association
Steve Smith                    The Lawrence Group
Tim Eby                        St. Louis Public Radio, 90.7 KWMU
Jack Galmiche                  Nine Network of Public Media
Vince Schoemehl                Grand Center Inc.
Don Stastny                    Stastny Architect

Project Team Members:
Dan Jay                        Christner
Laurel Harrington              Christner
Peter Schaudt                  Hoerr Schaudt Landscape Architects
Jon Brooke                     Hoerr Schaudt Landscape Architects
Rebeccah Bennett               Vector Communications

                   Vince, GCI: The corner of Spring and Olive is Mr. Foggy's property

                   the Scottish Rite parking lot. There's a parcel there that can be developed
                   and the Art Walk will move by it. We would like to examine if there is an
                   opportunity to put first floor retail in the Continental's garage as well as in
                   Big Brothers Big Sisters' building.

Spring Corridor Sub-Committee                                                 Grand Center
January 11, 2013 Discussion Summary                                     Great Streets Project

Overview
The Spring Corridor Sub-Committee met with members of the Great Streets (GS) team
on Thursday, January 10, 2013. Eleven committee members and Grand Center Inc.
(GCI) representatives participated in the meeting, which was held to accomplish the
following objectives:
    Acquaint committee members with the Great Streets team;
    Provide the team with information on the committee's work to date; and
    Identify critical corridor issues that the team needs to consider during the planning
    process.
A list of meeting attendees is presented below.

Overview
The Technical Advisory Group met with members of the Great Streets (GS) team on
Friday, January 11, 2013. Eleven committee members and Grand Center Inc. (GCI)
representatives participated in the meeting, which was held to accomplish the following
objectives:
    Acquaint committee members with the Great Streets team;

 Discussion Topic    Comments
  Meeting            Don, City of St. Louis:
  Purpose            Great Streets funding is a terrific overall planning context and flushed
                     things out at a high conceptual level and the technical advisory committee
                     group flowed from that. Planning and Urban Design often makes plans in a
                     vacuum and frequently there is a gotcha because they didn't problem solve
                     correctly. The TAG will help problem solve early.



                                                                                                  90
Discussion Focus Comments
 Meeting        Don, Framework Plan:
 Purpose        Thank you to members of the TAG for work on the Framework Plan. You
 Continued      were helpful with your input and the plan has set the stage for you all to
                look at different aspects that you will be dealing with in the future. The
                point is that you are a part of helping us and Grand Center going forward.
                Vince was able to secure a grant from East-West gateway and we plan to
                move the conceptual plan forward. The biggest part now is scoping the
                consultant's work that will start from the conceptual plan and move to a
                higher level, which is higher than what East-West gateway would normally
                see. I think the consultants have a good grasp of this. The consultant team
                has been going through a series of meetings. We met with those folks from
                Grand Center and other committees. We are kicking them off at a very high
                level and want the consultants to come to you for a high level start off.
                Vince, GCI:
                Thanks for your help during the Framework Plan. There are a couple of
                other grants we are working on, one from MSD through the EPA is being
                reviewed. Grand Center is looking at a Metrolink station at Grand that will
                hook into the Hodiamont track. This would create a loop from St. Vincent's
                park through the greenway to Hodiamont. GRG has committed $100,000 to
                develop conceptual plans for a bike path through SLU's campus to Grand.
                We are doing interviews with consultants on the 18th and will select
                quickly. Another grant is from the NEA for an Art Walk. We will select
                another consultant for this. Our hope is that within 4 weeks we will have all
                of these pieces decided and consolidated.
                Dan, Great Streets:
                We want to outline a process and schedule and discuss how we will engage
                the TAG. We want to anticipate infrastructure issues now rather than 18
                months from now. Lets integrate issues from all parties, which may come
                up in the next 20 years to work on now. We want constructive commentary
                on what we are planning and hope to engage in a discussion that reduces
                our number of surprises. Our effort to collect documentation is
                cumbersome, so any other anecdotal information that you are aware of
                about stormwater, traffic, or utilities is helpful.
                Laurel, Great Streets:
                We literally kicked off Monday evening. We had meetings yesterday with
                other committees. Our plan is to get smart about existing conditions until
                the end of February, beginning of March when we'll have an open charette
                meeting. We appreciate your time and will engage you again with notions
                of things and aesthetic choices. We will have diagrams of what we think
                and ask you for your feedback. Then we will really get into design and put
                things on paper. Following this, we'll engage you again to really dig into
                the details. We will be wrapping up the end of May with our report.

                For the new people, here's an overview. We are looking at Olive to Cook,
                with middle Grand as a transition at Lindell with SLU's campus. The
                Framework Plan has Grand as the major spine, Washington is the transept.




                                                                                                91
               Other streets are called corridors and boundaries of the district. Cook gets
               us up steeple to steeple. Green areas include the Art Walk, a possible
               greenway connection, a formal circus flora location with year round festival
               space for the district and greening the streets (i.e. midblock pedestrian
               connections). It's a very large district. Our primary focus is the street
               proper; there may be some connection points, but the biggest focus is the
               streets with land use opportunities. We are really looking for input on the
               street aspect. Where appropriate, we may widen sidewalks and narrow
               streets, protrusions, bio retentions and rain gardens. We are interested in
               what's under the streets and your plans for the future.

               Yesterday we heard about signal timing, fast speeds on Washington, signal
               timing for low vision or blind residents, lighting, and a lot of really good
               stuff. You have been working in this city for a really long time and have
               expertise that is invaluable to us.

               Dan, Great Streets:

Theresa Corridor Sub-Committee                                                Grand Center
January 10, 2013 Discussion Summary                                     Great Streets Project

Overview
The Theresa Corridor Sub-Committee met with members of the Great Streets (GS) team
on Thursday, January 10, 2013. Eleven committee members and Grand Center Inc.
(GCI) representatives participated in the meeting, which was held to accomplish the
following objectives:
    Acquaint committee members with the Great Streets team;
    Provide the team with information on the committee's work to date; and
    Identify critical corridor issues that the team needs to consider during the planning
    process.
A list of meeting attendees is presented below.

Washington Corridor Sub-Committee                                               Grand Center
January 10, 2013 Discussion Summary                                       Great Streets Project

Overview
The Washington Corridor Sub-Committee met with members of the Great Streets (GS)
team on Thursday, January 10, 2013. Fifteen committee members and Grand Center Inc.
(GCI) representatives participated in the meeting, which was held to accomplish the
following objectives:
    Acquaint committee members with the Great Streets team;
    Provide the team with information on the committee's work to date; and
    Identify critical corridor issues that the team needs to consider during the planning
    process.

Grand & Grandel Subcommittees Presentation                                Grand Center
April 5, 2013 Discussion Summary                                    Great Streets Project
Overview
Stakeholders from the Grand and Grandel Subcommittees met with members of the Great
Streets (GS) team on Friday, April 5, 2013. Sixteen committee members, Grand Center
Inc. (GCI) representatives and project officials participated in the meeting, which was
held to accomplish the following objectives:
    Provide information on the project team's work to date;
    Acquaint attendees with the team's design recommendations, with a focus on their
    impacts on the Grand and Grandel corridors; and
    Solicit stakeholder feedback on the recommendations.

Olive Subcommittee                                                         Grand Center
April 4, 2013 Discussion Summary                                     Great Streets Project

Overview
Stakeholders from the Grand Center District and surrounding environs met with members
of the Great Streets (GS) team on Thursday, April 4, 2013. Seventeen community
stakeholders, Grand Center Inc. (GCI) representatives and project officials participated in
the meeting, which was held to accomplish the following objectives:
    Provide information on the project team's work to date;
    Acquaint attendees with the team's design recommendations; and
    Solicit stakeholder feedback on the recommendations.

A list of meeting attendees is presented below.

Discussion Highlights

 Discussion Topic     Comments
  Lighting            Question: Are the lights staggered on the opposite sides of the
                      street?
                      Response: Yes
  Plants              Question: Will the plants in the planters be watered?
                      Response: Yes
  Lighting            Question: How does all of this new lighting mesh with the building
                      lighting that already exists?
                      Response: The flood lighting on the boulevard would only be used to
                      enhance buildings where it is needed. Also, by using the new low
                      bright light fixtures, we'll be able to see better the existing lighting,
                      on buildings. This means that there will be a heightened awareness
                      of building lighting.
  Stop Lights         Comment: Stop light length time is a real problem, especially on
                      Vandeventer, portions of Grand and Olive.
                      Response: On Vandeventer, the city is currently in the process of



                                                                                              136
                    trying to fix this issue. Contact Todd Waeltermann at the city about
                    the lights that present the greatest problems. He will help. The city
                    doesn't want public complaints and people unnecessarily held up.

Discussion Topic    Comments
 Alleys             Comment: The alleys can be exciting places, but they are also
                    places that people are afraid of. They are very prominent places in
                    Grand Center and fixing them up will go a long way to improving
                    Grand Center's appeal and making people feel safer.
 Plan               Question: What are your thoughts about the plan's costs and
   Implementation   scheduling?
                    Response: Once we refine our designs, we will be able to get good
                    cost estimates. This requires some additional work and meetings. We
                    will have to present costs for the plan's different phases, breaking the
                    estimates down so that they are not unwieldy. This is the work that
                    the core group will be doing next.
 Sustainability     Question: Are we looking at green options for lighting, like solar?
                    Response: We're looking at LED for reducing energy usage. Solar
                    gets tricky because shadows from the buildings make it less effective.
                    If we use LED lights, they are inherently dimmable and switchable.
                    This means that you can cut back output at different times of day and
                    thus curtail energy usage when its not needed.
                    Question: LED lights require how much energy?
                    Response: The advantage of LEDs is not that they are inherently
                    more efficient, but they are so "directable" and controllable that they
                    can double efficiency. There is an energy savings as a system of
                    anywhere from 20 % to 60%. These lights are only serviced
                    routinely a third as much as a conventional lighting sources.
 Lighting &         Question: How do you avoid conflicts between street trees and the
 Trees              lighting grid?
                    Response: It's all about maintenance. The conflict with the tree line
                    is manageable. The lighting grid is 35 feet high.
 Lighting           Question: Have the overhead lighting grid been installed in other
                    places?
                    Response: Not so much in the U.S. But, the grids have been
                    installed in Europe.
 Lighting           Comment: If we're going to get people to go to Compton and
                    Vandeventer, we're going to have to extend the lighting structure at
                    least to Washington Ave. So as we put this together, we're going to
                    have to figure out how we stretch this at least one block on the west
                    end and three blocks on the east end. If we just did it along
                    Washington and got people to Compton, this would be very helpful



                                                                                              137
in making people comfortable.
Response: Our document presents a set of design guidelines that can
be expanded or implemented as broadly as needed.

GREAT STREETS                                        PUBLIC OPEN HOUSE
GRAND CENTER                                      COMMENT FORM REPORT
TO:                   Grand Center Great Streets Project Team
FROM:                 Vector Communications Corp.
RE:                   Open House Comment Form Findings
PROJECT:              Great Streets Grand Center, Project 12082
DATE:                 March 13, 2013

Overview
On Thursday, February 28, 2013, Grand Center Great Streets hosted a public open house
from 6:00 pm to 8:00 pm at the Metropolitan Artists Lofts. One hundred and three
community members and District stakeholders attended this visioning session to discuss
their desires for neighborhood beautification, traffic, parking, streets, sidewalks and
more. Individually and in small groups, participants met with planners who listened to
their aspirations, issues and needs. These planners / project team members are now using
this information to design community solutions that enhance the quality of life in Grand
Center.
As part of the evening's activities, participants viewed open house boards that provided
information on the Great Streets principles, project goals, planning schedule and
analyses, and activities. These boards were clustered in themed stations that covered nine
topics, including:

       Great Streets and Framework Plan           Branding and Wayfinding
       Information
       Spatial Analysis                           Lighting
       Conditions                                 Public Art
       Stormwater                                 Street Sections
       Transportation

After participants toured the nine stations, they were invited to complete an event
comment form. This document asked them to provide basic information about
themselves; share how they learned about the event; evaluate their open house
experience; describe what would make the Great Streets project a success; and provide
additional comments or questions. Twenty-eight participants submitted completed
comment forms. The findings from their submissions have been compiled, aggregated
and summarized and are presented in this document for ease of reference and review.

Participant Background Information

Participants were asked to describe their connections to Grand Center. They were given
nine options from which to select and could choose multiple descriptors. Their answers
are presented in the table on the following page.




                                                                                          
                                                                                               151
  
1.    Which of the following best describes you? Please check all that apply.
            I live in or              I am a student or a parent of            I am a property
            near Grand                a student of a nearby school,            owner in Grand
      19%   Center            41%     college or university              0%    Center
            I work in or
            near Grand                I am a patron of the arts in             I worship in Grand
      19%   Center            48%     Grand Center                       7%    Center
            I shop and/or
            dine in Grand             I am a patient or visitor at the
      41%   Center            7%      Veterans' hospital                 15%   Other
Note: 27 people responded to this question.

Nearly half of those who completed comment forms identified themselves as patrons of
the arts. Forty-one percent also stated that they shop and/or dine in the District and are
either students or parents of students enrolled at institutions of learning in the District.
No property owners submitted comment forms, which could be because of their heavy
involvement in earlier charrette meetings.

Open House Outreach

A variety of outreach mechanisms were employed to generate awareness of and interest
in the public open house. Respondents were asked how they learned about the event to
help project team members identify the information channels that were most effective.
They were allowed to submit multiple responses as they may have been informed about
the event through multiple channels. The table below summarizes their responses.

2. How did you find out about this Open House? Please check all that apply.
      11%   Printed Flyer     33%     Email                              0%    Advertisement
      11%   Website           15%     Social Media / Facebook            41%   Word of Mouth
      0%    Newsletter        26%     Other
Note: 27 people responded to this question.

Respondents identified word of mouth and email as the primary means by which they
found out about the open house. Grand Center's printed flyers and various website
postings also attracted public notice. A little more than a quarter of respondents
identified "other" as their information source, but none provided a written explanation
that illuminated this response.

Event Evaluation

Participants were given the opportunity to comment on their experience of design team
members at the open house. They were asked to assess the extent to which team
members were informative, helpful and prepared using a five-point Likert scale. Using
the same scale, they were also invited to reflect on their overall experience of the open

scale. The average numerical finding is bolded and placed alongside its qualitative descriptor.

On the whole, participants who submitted comment forms found the design team to be
informative, helpful and prepared. They also maintained that the event overall was well
planned and worth their investment of time.

Open Ended Queries
The last part of the comment form presented open-ended questions that allowed
respondents to share their ideas and insights in depth. Two questions were presented for
consideration. The first inquired about what would make the Grand Center Great Streets
project a success. The second simply asked for additional comments or questions for
team review. The responses given to both questions have been unaltered and are bulleted

Conclusion

The information presented in this document will be reviewed by the design team and

GREAT STREETS                                            FINAL PRESENTATION
GRAND CENTER                                           COMMENT FORM REPORT
TO:                     Grand Center Great Streets Project Team
FROM:                   Vector Communications Corp.
RE:                     Final Presentation Comment Form Findings
PROJECT:                Great Streets Grand Center, Project 12082
DATE:                   May 17, 2013

Overview
On Thursday, May 9, 2013, Grand Center Great Streets hosted its final presentation
public meeting from 6:00 pm to 8:00 pm at Cardinal Ritter College Preparatory High
School. Seventy-four community members and District stakeholders attended this
meeting to review in detail the design team's recommendations for a more vibrant,
attractive Grand Center. Team members shared their proposed improvements for lighting,
parking, streets and sidewalks, landscaping and beautification, traffic flow, and bicycle
and transit access.
Every member of the project team participated in the 90-minute presentation, which was
followed by a 30-minute question and answer session. The presentation included:

         An overview of Great Streets' principles,
         A synopsis of Grand Center vision statements,
         A summary of the public engagement program,
         Digital survey results,
         An exploration of redevelopment opportunities,
         Streetscape and lighting recommendations,
         A vision of public art in the District, along with guiding principles and strategies,
         Suggested storwmater treatments and best management practices,
         A listing of branding, signage and wayfinding opportunities, and
         Insights on changing travel habits to, from and through Grand Center.

At the meeting's end, meeting participants were invited to complete an event comment
form. This document asked them to provide basic information about themselves; share
how they learned about the event; evaluate their public meeting experience; give their
feedback on the proposed designs; and provide additional comments or questions.
Twenty-five participants submitted completed comment forms. The findings from their
submissions have been compiled and summarized and are presented in this document for
ease of reference and review.

Participant Background Information

Participants were asked to describe their connections to Grand Center. They were given
nine options from which to select and could choose multiple descriptors. Their answers
are presented in the table on the following page.

1.    Which of the following best describes you? Please check all that apply.

            I work in or
            near Grand               I am a patron of the arts in             I worship in Grand

            I shop and/or
            dine in Grand            I am a patient or visitor at the
      36%   Center            0%     Veterans' hospital                 12%   Other
Note: Respondents were able to select more than one option.

Sixty percent of those who completed comment forms identified themselves as patrons of
the arts. Thirty-six percent also stated that they shop and/or dine in the District and work
in or near Grand Center. And, close to 30% indicated that they either live in or near
Grand Center.

Final Presentation Outreach

A variety of outreach mechanisms were employed to generate awareness of and interest
in the final presentation. Respondents were asked how they learned about the event to
help project team members identify the information channels that were most effective.
They were allowed to submit multiple responses as they may have been informed about

GREAT STREETS                                                        FINAL PRESENTATION
GRAND CENTER                                                        PUBLIC MEETING Q & A
Date:                       Thursday, May 9, 2013
Time:                       5:00 p.m. to 8:00 p.m.
Location:                   Cardinal Ritter College Preparatory High School
Attendees:                  Members of the Public
Meeting Purpose:            Public Meeting
Project:                    Great Streets Grand Center
Project Number:             12082
                                                          
Overview  
The  following  pages  contain  a  summary  of  the  questions  and  comments  made  by  
members  of  the  public  at  the  Thursday,  May  9th  Grand  Center  Great  Streets  public  
open  house.    


      1. Comment: I love the overall concept presented tonight, but what concerns me
         greatly is that the prime gateway to the neighborhood ­ Grand and Lindell ­ is
         getting very little attention. The fact that the team is not pushing SLU to do
         something with this gateway is problematic. This is a high density corner and
         really should be developed as more than a sculpture park. The team's large
         efforts are undermined without that corner being developed. It remains negative
         space and you're losing an opportunity to brand the prime entry into the
         neighborhood.
      2. Comment: I'm not an urban planner, but to me Grand Center is not a warm
         space. In your presentation it just looks like you're doctoring up the coldness of
         Grand. You should consider closing the thoroughfare and making it a pedestrian
         walkway. Be disruptive and take big steps.
      3. Comment & Question: You're going to redo the park at Grand and Washington.
         What are you going to do with the existing statues and Bible stand? There are a
         lot of disabled people who live along this corridor. The city's already taking bus
         stops out. What's the reasoning for this? And what will be done in the future?
         Response: The existing elements in the park can be worked into a new design. It
         is our intention to leave them there. As for the buses, there is a proposal from
         Metro to look at the bus stops and to change where they are located to
         accommodate the larger buses that are coming on line. New stops are proposed
         south of Olive and flanking Enright.
      4. Comment & Question: I have occasion to use the bus stops and the locations
         you mention that are being proposed are farther apart than the existing ones. On
         another note, can you tell me about this park that's being developed in
         cooperation with the Pulitzer and Washington University?
         Response: The "park" is actually not a permanent project; it's a temporary
         installation that's called the Pixel. It is a design competition for artisan designers
         to create temporary pavilion spaces. My understanding is that it will be open to


                                                                                                                 
                                                                                                                      162
         the public in 2014. To my knowledge it would not necessarily be an ongoing
         program. The reason it is there is because it is on land owned by the Pulitzer
         Foundation and it is a project of the museum.
      5. Comment: We need a plaza that focuses on the Sheldon.
      6. Question: Where is the site that you are discussing now?
         Response: It is on Washington Boulevard, across the street from the Pulitzer and
         next to Bruno.
      7. Question: How far north are the new lights going to go?
         Response: The lights would go from Lindell on the south to Cook on the north.
      8. Comment: I think your porous pavement is a great idea in terms of stormwater
         management, but it will provide a major headache for all of your street trees with
         all of the salt that the city uses in the winter.
         Response: You're right, this can happen when it sits, but the pavers that we are
         proposing have a flushing action. Detailing can address some of your concern.
